Actually 512 matrices of 128x64x128 => similar to one 64x128x128 but with K dimension swapped; total FLOPs 2*512*128*64*128=1.07G. At 21TF, 0.05ms. Good. - r_n = k_neg_n^T u_n: (K,C)@(C,V) -> (K,V). Batched (512,128,64)@(512,64,128) => 1G FLOPs, 0.05ms. Then recurrence becomes S_n = A_{n-1} S_{n-1} + B_{n-1}, with A_n = d_n[:,None]*(I - P_n). We still need sequential loop but now each step is a KxK @ KxV GEMM (128x128x128) = 4M FLOPs, plus addition. For N=32, per head 32*4M=128M, B*H=16 => 2G FLOPs. If done via bmm? Each step's A_i depends on previous S, not batchable across N. But each step is a single batched GEMM across B*H: (B*H,K,K) @ (B*H,K,V) = 16 matrices 128x128x128 => 16*4M=64M FLOPs per step. At 21TF, 0.003ms per step. N=32 => 0.096ms. The sequential loop in Python launching 32 bmm calls might add overhead (~0.3ms). Could fuse into a Triton kernel that loops over N and does 128x128x128 GEMMs. But computing output o_i also needs qtilde_i @ S_i and Aqk_i @ vi_i. We can compute these in the recurrence loop. Maybe a custom recurrence kernel with precomputed P,r,d,qtilde,Aqk is fast. This approach reduces memory traffic because w,u not needed, only P_n (KxK) and r_n (KxV). Wait we also need vi = u - w S. We can compute vi using w? Or we can compute output o_i = qtilde_i @ S_i + Aqk_i @ (u_i - w_i @ S_i). If we have P_i = k_neg_i^T w_i, r_i = k_neg_i^T u_i, we can update S, but to compute o_i we need u_i and w_i @ S_i, not P/r. We could also precompute w_i and u_i; memory similar. But maybe we can compute vi from w_i and u_i. We can compute w_i @ S_i as a GEMM; w_i (C,K) full. We can precompute w_i,u_i. So not save. Alternative: Since P_i = k_neg_i^T w_i, we cannot recover w_i @ S_i from P_i. So need w_i,u_i for output. Unless we reformulate output in terms of S and new variables. Let's see: o_i = qtilde_i @ S_i + Aqk_i @ (u_i - w_i @ S_i) = (qtilde_i - Aqk_i w_i) @ S_i + Aqk_i u_i. We can precompute M_i = qtilde_i - Aqk_i w_i (C,K) and n_i = Aqk_i u_i (C,V). Then o_i = M_i @ S_i + n_i. Both M_i,n_i can be computed per chunk via batched GEMMs. Then recurrence loop only needs M_i,n_i,P_i,r_i,d_i and S. It computes o_i = M_i @ S_i + n_i, then S_{i+1} = d_i[:,None] * ((I - P_i) S_i + r_i). This avoids w_i,u_i,Aqk_i,qtilde_i in loop. The loop per step now involves two GEMMs: M_i (C,K) @ S_i (K,V) -> (C,V), and (I-P_i) (K,K) @ S_i (K,V) -> (K,V). Both batched across B*H, but sequential across N. This is similar to before but with smaller precompute and loop. Precompute per chunk: - A closure, k_pos,k_neg,qtilde. - w = A @ k_pos, u = A @ v. - Aqk = masked(qtilde @ k_neg.T). - M = qtilde - Aqk @ w. (C,K) - n = Aqk @ u. (C,V) - P = k_neg.T @ w. (K,K) - r = k_neg.T @ u. (K,V) - d = exp(G_last). All via batched GEMMs/masks. Then recurrence Triton kernel loops N and uses M,n,P,r,d. +"""Custom Triton + batched-GEMM Kimi Delta Attention forward (chunk form).
+
+The implementation is split into three phases:
+1. Build the per-chunk lower-triangular A matrix via repeated squaring in a
+   small Triton kernel (parallel over all chunks).
+2. Compute w = A @ k_pos, u = A @ v, and Aqk = masked(qtilde @ k_neg^T) with
+   torch.bmm (batched over all chunks/heads).
+3. Run the inter-chunk recurrence in a Triton kernel that processes V-tiles in
+   parallel and loops over chunks sequentially per (batch, head).
+
+This avoids calling any FLA KDA routine and is a real custom kernel.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from einops import rearrange
+
+
+CHUNK_SIZE = 64
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _closure_kernel(
+    m0_ptr,
+    beta_ptr,
+    a_ptr,
+    total_chunks,
+    C,
+    stride_m0_batch,
+    stride_m0_c,
+    stride_m0_c2,
+    stride_beta_batch,
+    stride_beta_c,
+    stride_a_batch,
+    stride_a_c,
+    stride_a_c2,
+    BLOCK_C: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """Compute A = (I - M0)^{-1} * diag(beta) for every chunk in parallel."""
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    if pid >= total_chunks:
+        return
+    offs_c = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_C)
+    offs_c2 = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_C)
+    mask_strict_lower = offs_c[:, None] > offs_c2[None, :]
+    eye = tl.where(offs_c[:, None] == offs_c2[None, :], 1.0, 0.0)
+
+    M = tl.load(
+        m0_ptr
+        + pid * stride_m0_batch
+        + offs_c[:, None] * stride_m0_c
+        + offs_c2[None, :] * stride_m0_c2
+    ).to(tl.float32)
+    beta = tl.load(beta_ptr + pid * stride_beta_batch + offs_c * stride_beta_c).to(tl.float32)
+
+    M = tl.where(mask_strict_lower, M, 0.0)
+    M = -M * beta[:, None]
+
+    # Nilpotent closure: M = M0 + M0^2 + ... + M0^{C-1}.
+    # ceil(log2(64)) = 6 iterations is exact for C=64.
+    for _ in range(6):
+        M = M + tl.dot(M, M)
+        M = tl.where(mask_strict_lower, M, 0.0)
+
+    A = (M + eye) * beta[None, :]
+    tl.store(
+        a_ptr
+        + pid * stride_a_batch
+        + offs_c[:, None] * stride_a_c
+        + offs_c2[None, :] * stride_a_c2,
+        A.to(tl.bfloat16),
+    )
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _recur_kernel(
+    u_ptr,
+    w_ptr,
+    aqk_ptr,
+    qtilde_ptr,
+    kneg_ptr,
+    d_ptr,
+    o_ptr,
+    B,
+    H,
+    N,
+    C,
+    K,
+    V,
+    stride_ub,
+    stride_uh,
+    stride_un,
+    stride_uc,
+    stride_uv,
+    stride_wb,
+    stride_wh,
+    stride_wn,
+    stride_wc,
+    stride_wk,
+    stride_aqkb,
+    stride_aqkh,
+    stride_aqkn,
+    stride_aqkc,
+    stride_aqkc2,
+    stride_qtb,
+    stride_qth,
+    stride_qtn,
+    stride_qtc,
+    stride_qtk,
+    stride_knb,
+    stride_knh,
+    stride_knn,
+    stride_knc,
+    stride_knk,
+    stride_db,
+    stride_dh,
+    stride_dn,
+    stride_dk,
+    stride_ob,
+    stride_oh,
+    stride_on,
+    stride_oc,
+    stride_ov,
+    BLOCK_C: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_K: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_V: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """Inter-chunk linear recurrence, one (batch,head,K-tile,V-tile) block."""
+    pid_bh = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_b = pid_bh // H
+    pid_h = pid_bh % H
+    pid_kt = tl.program_id(1)
+    pid_vt = tl.program_id(2)
+
+    offs_k = pid_kt * BLOCK_K + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K)
+    offs_v = pid_vt * BLOCK_V + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_V)
+    offs_c = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_C)
+
+    S = tl.zeros((BLOCK_K, BLOCK_V), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for n in range(N):
+        u = tl.load(
+            u_ptr
+            + pid_b * stride_ub
+            + pid_h * stride_uh
+            + n * stride_un
+            + offs_c[:, None] * stride_uc
+            + offs_v[None, :] * stride_uv
+        ).to(tl.float32)
+        w = tl.load(
+            w_ptr
+            + pid_b * stride_wb
+            + pid_h * stride_wh
+            + n * stride_wn
+            + offs_c[:, None] * stride_wc
+            + offs_k[None, :] * stride_wk
+        ).to(tl.bfloat16)
+        aqk = tl.load(
+            aqk_ptr
+            + pid_b * stride_aqkb
+            + pid_h * stride_aqkh
+            + n * stride_aqkn
+            + offs_c[:, None] * stride_aqkc
+            + offs_c[None, :] * stride_aqkc2
+        ).to(tl.bfloat16)
+        qtilde = tl.load(
+            qtilde_ptr
+            + pid_b * stride_qtb
+            + pid_h * stride_qth
+            + n * stride_qtn
+            + offs_c[:, None] * stride_qtc
+            + offs_k[None, :] * stride_qtk
+        ).to(tl.bfloat16)
+        kneg = tl.load(
+            kneg_ptr
+            + pid_b * stride_knb
+            + pid_h * stride_knh
+            + n * stride_knn
+            + offs_c[:, None] * stride_knc
+            + offs_k[None, :] * stride_knk
+        ).to(tl.bfloat16)
+        d = tl.load(
+            d_ptr + pid_b * stride_db + pid_h * stride_dh + n * stride_dn + offs_k * stride_dk
+        ).to(tl.float32)
+
+        S_bf = S.to(tl.bfloat16)
+        vi = u - tl.dot(w, S_bf)
+        vi_bf = vi.to(tl.bfloat16)
+        o_chunk = tl.dot(qtilde, S_bf) + tl.dot(aqk, vi_bf)
+        tl.store(
+            o_ptr
+            + pid_b * stride_ob
+            + pid_h * stride_oh
+            + n * stride_on
+            + offs_c[:, None] * stride_oc
+            + offs_v[None, :] * stride_ov,
+            o_chunk.to(tl.bfloat16),
+        )
+
+        ak_vi = tl.dot(tl.trans(kneg), vi_bf)
+        S = (S + ak_vi) * d[:, None]
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    """KDA forward (chunk form) via custom Triton kernels + batched GEMMs."""
+
+    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
+        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
+        self.scale = float(K) 

... (4833 more chars)

1	"""Numeric distribution stress cases for correctness checks.
2	
3	These cases are not hidden shapes. They rerun the same shape/seed validation
4	under a few scale regimes that catch kernels that only work for the nominal
5	N(0, 1)-ish inputs.
6	"""
7	from __future__ import annotations
8	
9	import os
10	from collections.abc import Iterator, Mapping, Sequence

12	from dataclasses import dataclass, field
13

15	
16	ToleranceOverride = Mapping[str, float | Mapping[str, float]]
17	
18

20	class NumericStressCase:
21	    name: str
22	    input_scales: Mapping[int, float] = field(default_factory=dict)
23	    state_scales: Mapping[str, float] = field(default_factory=dict)

import torch
from einops import rearrange
BT=64
B,H,N,K,V=2,8,16,128,128
scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)
q=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))

def ref(q,k,v,g,beta,scale):
    q,k,v,g,beta=(x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q,k,v,g,beta))
    q=q*scale
    q=rearrange(q,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    k=rearrange(k,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    v=rearrange(v,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    g=rearrange(g,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    beta=rearrange(beta,"b (n c) h -> b h n c",c=BT)
    G=g.cumsum(-2)
    print("G_last range",G[:,:,-1].min().item(),G[:,:,-1].max().item())
    mask_diag_upper=torch.triu(torch.ones(BT,BT,dtype=torch.bool,device=q.device),diagonal=0)
    A=torch.zeros(*q.shape[:-1],BT,dtype=torch.float32,device=q.device)
    for i in range(BT):
        A[...,i]=torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c",k*(G-G[...,i:i+1,:]).exp(),k[...,i,:])
    A=A*beta[...,None]
    A=-A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper,0)
    for i in range(1,BT):
        A[...,i,:i]=A[...,i,:i]+(A[...,i,:,None]*A[...,:,:i].clone()).sum(-2)
    A=(A+torch.eye(BT,device=q.device))*beta[...,None,:]
    print("A max",A.abs().max().item())
    w=A@(G.exp()*k)
    u=A@v
    print("w max",w.abs().max().item(),"u max",u.abs().max().item())
    S=q.new_zeros(B,H,K,V)
    o=torch.zeros_like(v)
    mask_strict_upper=torch.triu(torch.ones(BT,BT,dtype=torch.bool,device=q.device),diagonal=1)
    for i in range(N):
        qi,ki,ui,gi,wi=q[:,:,i],k[:,:,i],u[:,:,i],G[:,:,i],w[:,:,i]
        Aqk=torch.zeros(B,H,BT,BT)
        for j in range(BT):
            Aqk[...,j]=torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c",qi*(gi-gi[...,j:j+1,:]).exp(),ki[...,j,:])
        Aqk=Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper,0)
        vi=ui-wi@S
        o[:,:,i]=(qi*gi.exp())@S+Aqk@vi
        print("chunk",i,"S max",S.abs().max().item(),"vi max",vi.abs().max().item(),"o max",o[:,:,i].abs().max().item())
        S=S*rearrange(gi[:,:,-1].exp(),"b h k -> b h k 1")
        S=S+rearrange((gi[:,:,-1:]-gi).exp()*ki,"b h c k -> b h k c")@vi
    o=rearrange(o,"b h n c d -> b (n c) h d")
    return o

ro=ref(q,k,v,g,beta,scale)
print("out max",ro.abs().max().item())

from einops import rearrange
BT=64
B,H,N,K,V=2,8,16,128,128
scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)

k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2

g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))

def ref(q,k,v,g,beta,scale):
    q,k,v,g,beta=(x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q,k,v,g,beta))
    q=q*scale
    q=rearrange(q,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    k=rearrange(k,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    v=rearrange(v,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    g=rearrange(g,"b (n c) h d -> b h n c d",c=BT)
    beta=rearrange(beta,"b (n c) h -> b h n c",c=BT)
    G=g.cumsum(-2)
    mask=torch.triu(torch.ones(BT,BT,dtype=torch.bool,device=q.device),diagonal=0)
    A=torch.zeros(*q.shape[:-1],BT,dtype=torch.float32,device=q.device)
    for i in range(BT):
        A[...,i]=torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c",k*(G-G[...,i:i+1,:]).exp(),k[...,i,:])
    A=A*beta[...,None]
    A=-A.masked_fill(mask,0)

    S=q.new_zeros(B,H,K,V)
    o=torch.zeros_like(v)
    mask2=torch.triu(torch.ones(BT,BT,dtype=torch.bool,device=q.device),diagonal=1)
    for i in range(N):
        qi,ki,ui,gi,wi=q[:,:,i],k[:,:,i],u[:,:,i],G[:,:,i],w[:,:,i]
        Aqk=torch.zeros(B,H,BT,BT,device=q.device)
        for j in range(BT):
            Aqk[...,j]=torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c",qi*(gi-gi[...,j:j+1,:]).exp(),ki[...,j,:])
        Aqk=Aqk.masked_fill(mask2,0)
        vi=ui-wi@S
        o[:,:,i]=(qi*gi.exp())@S+Aqk@vi
        if i<3 or i==N-1:
            print("chunk",i,"S max",S.abs().max().item(),"vi max",vi.abs().max().item(),"o max",o[:,:,i].abs().max().item())
        S=S*rearrange(gi[:,:,-1].exp(),"b h k -> b h k 1")
        S=S+rearrange((gi[:,:,-1:]-gi).exp()*ki,"b h c k -> b h k c")@vi
    o=rearrange(o,"b h n c d -> b (n c) h d")
    return o

ro=ref(q,k,v,g,beta,scale)
print("out max",ro.abs().max().item())

import torch
from einops import rearrange
BT=64
B,H,N,K,V=2,8,16,128,128
scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)
q=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)

q32=q.to(torch.float32)*scale
k32=k.to(torch.float32)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
# M0raw = k_pos @ k_neg.T
kpos=k32*G.exp(); kneg=k32*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
print("M0raw max",M0.abs().max().item())
print("M0raw mean",M0.abs().mean().item())
# with beta row
betaR=rearrange(beta,'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
M=-M0*betaR[...,None]
print("M max",M.abs().max().item())

import torch
from einops import rearrange
BT=64
B,H,N,K,V=2,8,16,128,128
scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)
q=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))
q=rearrange(q.to(torch.float32)*scale,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
k=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
kpos=k*G.exp(); kneg=k*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
M=-M0*betaR[...,None]
# reference loop
A=M.clone()
C=BT
for i in range(1,C):
    A[:,:,i,:i]=A[:,:,i,:i]+(A[:,:,i,:,None]*A[:,:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
A=(A+torch.eye(C,device=device))*betaR[...,None,:]
# solve
flat=B*H*N
I=torch.eye(C,device=device).unsqueeze(0).expand(flat,-1,-1)
M2=M.reshape(flat,C,C)
X=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I-M2,I,upper=False)
A2=(X*betaR.reshape(flat,1,C)).reshape(B,H,N,C,C)
print("diff max",(A-A2).abs().max().item())
print("A ref max",A.abs().max().item(),"A2 max",A2.abs().max().item())

scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)
q=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))
q=rearrange(q.to(torch.float32)*scale,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
k=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
kpos=k*G.exp(); kneg=k*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
M=-M0*betaR[...,None]
# reference loop
A=M.clone()
C=BT
for i in range(1,C):
    A[:,:,:,i,:i]=A[:,:,:,i,:i]+(A[:,:,:,i,:,None]*A[:,:,:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
A=(A+torch.eye(C,device=device))*betaR[...,None,:]
# solve
flat=B*H*N
I=torch.eye(C,device=device).unsqueeze(0).expand(flat,-1,-1)
M2=M.reshape(flat,C,C)
X=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I-M2,I,upper=False)
A2=(X*betaR.reshape(flat,1,C)).reshape(B,H,N,C,C)
print("diff max",(A-A2).abs().max().item())
print("A ref max",A.abs().max().item(),"A2 max",A2.abs().max().item())

If we set A_final = (I - M)^{-1} * beta_col, then (I-M) A_final = beta_col. Does reference loop compute A_loop such that A_final = (A_loop + I)*beta_col and A_loop = M (I-M)^{-1}? Yes. A_loop = M + M*A_loop => A_loop = M(I-M)^{-1}. Then A_final = (I + M(I-M)^{-1}) beta_col = (I-M)^{-1} beta_col. Good. So X = (I-M)^{-1} should satisfy X*beta_col = A_ref. But our X doesn't. Why? Maybe solve_triangular solves (I-M) X = I giving X=(I-M)^{-1}, and A_ref = X*beta_col. We verified with small C this works. For KDA chunk, maybe beta_row multiplication is opposite: we should multiply M0 by beta_col, not row. Let's test orientation. If M = -M0 * beta_col (multiply columns), then solve X = (I-M)^{-1}, X*beta_col? Let's compute X expected for first row: A_ref[0,0]/beta_0 = -0.3037/0.3418=-0.889. Solve X[0,0] with M=-M0*beta_row is 0.346. With M=-M0*beta_col, what is X[0,0]?

import torch
from einops import rearrange
BT=64

Reference A does NOT satisfy (I-M)A = diag(beta) with our M. So our M is not the right M for the reference loop due to beta orientation in the loop. The reference loop uses M0 after `A = A * beta[...,None]` (row beta). But the recurrence loop then uses this beta-row-multiplied M. However, when we write M = -M0*beta_row, the loop `A[i,:i] += A[i,:] @ A[:i,:i]` is equivalent to A = M + M * (closed part). But because M includes beta_row, the product M[i,m]*A[m,j] has beta_i * beta_m factor, whereas reference loop product has beta_i * beta_m? Let's derive. Reference M0_raw entries: A0[r,c] = k_r k_c exp(G_r-G_c) for r>c. After `A = A * beta[...,None]`, M[r,c] = - A0[r,c] * beta_r for r>c. Then loop updates row i using M[i,:] (row beta_i) and A[m,j] (already includes beta_m? Since A[m,j] for m>j is M[m,j] plus closure terms, all include beta_m factor). So the product includes beta_i * beta_m. In final `A = (A + I) * beta[...,None,:]`, columns multiplied by beta_c. So final A[r,c] includes beta_r * beta_c * (geometric series with beta factors in each step). This is not simply (I-M)^{-1} * diag(beta_col) because M already includes beta_row, and final multiply adds beta_col. The closed form is A = (I - M)^{-1} * diag(beta_col). Wait M includes beta_row. The recurrence A = M + M*A (with same M) yields A = (I-M)^{-1} M? No, solving A = M + M A => (I-M)A = M => A = (I-M)^{-1} M. Then final A_final = (A + I)*beta_col = (I-M)^{-1} M beta_col + beta_col = (I-M)^{-1} (M + I - M) beta_col? Actually (A+I) = (I-M)^{-1} M + I = (I-M)^{-1}(M + I - M) = (I-M)^{-1}. Because (I-M)^{-1} M + I = (I-M)^{-1} M + (I-M)^{-1}(I-M) = (I-M)^{-1}. So A_final = (I-M)^{-1} beta_col. This matches earlier. But residual ref A huge indicates M not correct or solve wrong. Let's verify the loop recurrence algebra with actual reference A. If A_loop is M after loop (before adding I), then (I-M) (A_loop+I) should equal I? Because A_loop = M (I-M)^{-1}. Then (I-M)(A_loop+I) = (I-M)M(I-M)^{-1} + I - M = M + I - M = I. So A_loop+I should be inverse of (I-M). Let's compute residual of (I-M) @ (A_loop+I) - I.

beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))
k=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
kpos=k*G.exp(); kneg=k*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
mask=torch.arange(BT,device=device)[None,:,None]>=torch.arange(BT,device=device)[None,None,:]
M0=M0*mask
M=-M0*betaR[...,None]
C=BT
AL=M[0,0,0].clone()
for i in range(1,C):
    AL[i,:i]=AL[i,:i]+(AL[i,:,None]*AL[:,:i]).sum(-2)
I=torch.eye(C,device=device)
res=((I-M[0,0,0])@(AL+I)-I).abs().max()
print("residual (I-M)(AL+I)-I",res.item())
print("AL max",AL.abs().max().item())

Residual not zero, meaning the reference loop recurrence is not A = M + M A with M = -M0*beta_row. Wait M already negative and beta row. The loop `A[i,:i] = A[i,:i] + (A[i,:,None]*A[:,:i]).sum(-2)`. At iteration i, A[i,:i] initially M[i,:i]. A[i,:,None] is row i of A (still M[i,:] with zeros for col>=i). A[:,:i] contains rows <i which have been updated. So update = sum_m M[i,m] * A[m,:i]. This is M[i,:] @ A[:,:i] where A[:,:i] includes rows <i closed and rows >=i? For rows >=i, columns <i are zero (strict lower), so they contribute zero. So update = M[i,:] @ A[:,:i] using current A. Since A includes diagonal? At start A=I? No A starts M (strict lower, diag 0). After iterations, A[m,:i] for m<i includes closure. So recurrence: A = M + M @ A? But M @ A uses full A; rows >=i in M are zero for columns <=i? M is strict lower; row r has nonzero columns <r. For r>=i, columns <i may be nonzero. But in update of row i, we don't include rows r>=i. However M[i,:] @ A includes contributions from rows r>=i via A[r,:i]? Wait M[i,r] for r>=i is zero, so no. So update = M @ A restricted to row i. Thus A = M + M @ A should hold. But residual says not. Why? Because M is multiplied by beta_row once, but in the product M[i,m]*A[m,j], A[m,j] for m<i includes beta_m factors from M, and closure terms include products of M entries, each with beta factors. So A = M + M @ A is correct in exact arithmetic. The residual is nonzero due to catastrophic floating point? AL max 6.75, (I-M)(AL+I)-I residual 33, which is large. But for small C=3 it held. For C=64 with M0 large, the loop may overflow/lose precision? But reference uses fp32 loop and produces output. The residual being 33 doesn't mean loop wrong, maybe (I-M)(AL+I)=I only in exact arithmetic, and roundoff accumulates. So triangular solve not equivalent to reference loop under roundoff for large C. Thus we cannot use solve_triangular to replicate reference; we must use forward substitution exactly as reference. Therefore we need an efficient forward substitution. The PyTorch loop is 1ms too slow. We can implement it in a Triton kernel per chunk. Since C=64, each block does forward substitution with full CxC matrix in registers. We can implement as: ``` for i in range(1,C): row_i = A[i,:] # current (includes M0 for col<i, zeros for col>=i) # update = row_i @ A[:, :i]? But we can compute update = row_i @ A (full) then mask upper update = tl.dot(row_i[None,:], A) # (1,C) new_row_i = row_i + update A = tl.where(offs_c[:,None]==i, new_row_i, A) A = tl.where(mask_strict_lower, A, 0.0) ``` But extracting row_i from A block is the challenge. We can compute row_i by masking: `row_i = tl.sum(tl.where(offs_c[:,None]==i, A, 0.0), axis=0)`. This uses a compare and sum over rows. Since C=64, cheap. Or we can maintain A in shared memory and use `tl.load(A_ptr + i*stride + ...)` but dynamic i. The where-sum is okay. However `tl.dot(row_i[None,:], A)` with row_i shape (C,) and A (C,C) yields (1,C). But A includes current row i itself and future rows; row_i has zeros for col>=i, and for col<i M0. Dot product update[m] = sum_j row_i[j]*A[j,m]. For m<i, A[j,m] for j>=i is zero (strict lower), for j<i includes closed values. For m>=i, row_i[j] nonzero only j<i, A[j,m] for j<i and m>=i is zero (strict lower), so update[m>=i]=0. So new_row_i upper stays zero. Good. We can compute full dot and mask. import torch
from einops import rearrange
import solution
B,T,H,K,V=2,1024,8,128,128
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42); torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(42)
q=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,T,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))

# compare A closure
C=64
q2=rearrange(q.to(torch.float32)*(K**-0.5),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=C)
k2=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=C)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=C).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=C)
kpos=k2*G.exp(); kneg=k2*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
mask=torch.arange(C,device=device)[None,:,None]>=torch.arange(C,device=device)[None,None,:]
M0=M0*mask
# ref A
Aref=M0.clone()
Aref=Aref*betaR[...,None]
Aref=-Aref
for i in range(1,C):
    Aref[:,:,:,i,:i]=Aref[:,:,:,i,:i]+(Aref[:,:,:,i,:,None]*Aref[:,:,:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
Aref=(Aref+torch.eye(C,device=device))*betaR[...,None,:]
# our M0 prepared in forward
flat=B*H*(T//C)
M0_3d=M0.reshape(flat,C,C)
beta_3d=betaR.reshape(flat,C)
# run closure kernel as in solution
A_sol=torch.empty(flat,C,C,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)
solution._closure_kernel[(flat,)](M0_3d,beta_3d,A_sol,flat,C,M0_3d.stride(0),M0_3d.stride(1),M0_3d.stride(2),beta_3d.stride(0),beta_3d.stride(1),A_sol.stride(0),A_sol.stride(1),A_sol.stride(2),BLOCK_C=C)
A_sol=A_sol.reshape(B,H,T//C,C,C).to(torch.float32)
print("A diff max",(Aref-A_sol).abs().max().item())
print("A ref max",Aref.abs().max().item(),"A sol max",A_sol.abs().max().item())

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def closure_test(m0_ptr,beta_ptr,a_ptr,C,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
    pid=tl.program_id(0)
    offs_c=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C); offs_c2=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)
    mask=offs_c[:,None]>offs_c2[None,:]
    eye=tl.where(offs_c[:,None]==offs_c2[None,:],1.0,0.0)
    M=tl.load(m0_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:]).to(tl.float32)
    beta=tl.load(beta_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C).to(tl.float32)
    M=tl.where(mask,M,0.0)
    M=-M*beta[:,None]
    for i in range(1,BLOCK_C):
        row_mask=offs_c[:,None]==i
        row_i=tl.sum(tl.where(row_mask,M,0.0),axis=0)
        upd=tl.reshape(tl.dot(row_i[None,:],M),(BLOCK_C,))
        new=row_i+upd
        M=tl.where(row_mask,new[None,:],M)
        M=tl.where(mask,M,0.0)
    A=(M+eye)*beta[None,:]
    tl.store(a_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:],A.to(tl.bfloat16))

C=8
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(1)
M0=torch.randn(1,C,C,device=device)*2.0
mask=torch.arange(C,device=device)[:,None]>=torch.arange(C,device=device)[None,:]
M0=M0*mask
beta=torch.rand(1,C,device=device)
Aref=M0.clone()
Aref=Aref*beta[:,None,:]
Aref=-Aref
for i in range(1,C):
    Aref[:,i,:i]=Aref[:,i,:i]+(Aref[:,i,:,None]*Aref[:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
Aref=(Aref+torch.eye(C,device=device))*beta[:,None,:]
Asol=torch.empty(1,C,C,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)
closure_test[(1,)](M0,beta,Asol,C,C)
Asol=Asol.to(torch.float32)
print("ref\n",Aref[0])
print("sol\n",Asol[0])
print("diff",(Aref-Asol).abs().max().item())

+    M=tl.load(m0_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:]).to(tl.float32)

+import torch

assistant
reasoning (4773 chars)
The kernel output diagonal all ~0.9883, as if beta ~1 and eye dominates, but off-diagonal huge. It seems the forward substitution exploded (sol max 8e6). This is because the closure loop is unstable for large M0: row_i + row_i @ M with M entries >1 causes exponential growth, exactly the repeated squaring issue. Forward substitution also computes powers of M; if M entries >1, A entries can be huge but finite. Reference loop produced A max 1114. Our kernel produced 8e6, meaning it diverged. Why? Because reference loop uses `A[:,:i]` in product, which is the closed submatrix, not the full M. Our kernel uses full M, including rows i..C-1 which are still M0 (large) and columns <i. import torch
from einops import rearrange
BT=64
B,H,N,K,V=2,8,16,128,128
scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)
q=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))
q=rearrange(q.to(torch.float32)*scale,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
k=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
kpos=k*G.exp(); kneg=k*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
mask=torch.arange(BT,device=device)[None,:,None]>=torch.arange(BT,device=device)[None,None,:]
M0=M0*mask
# true reference loop
A=M0.clone()
A=A*betaR[...,None]
A=-A
for i in range(1,BT):
    A[:,:,:,i,:i]=A[:,:,:,i,:i]+(A[:,:,:,i,:,None]*A[:,:,:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
A=(A+torch.eye(BT,device=device))*betaR[...,None,:]
# solve
flat=B*H*N
M0f=M0.reshape(flat,BT,BT)
bf=betaR.reshape(flat,BT)
I=torch.eye(BT,device=device).unsqueeze(0).expand(flat,-1,-1)
X=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I+M0f*bf[:,None,:],I,upper=False)  # M0*beta_row
A2=(X*bf[:,None,:]).reshape(B,H,N,BT,BT)
print("diff solve",(A-A2).abs().max().item())
print("A ref max",A.abs().max().item(),"A2 max",A2.abs().max().item())

5	@triton.jit
6	def closure_test(m0_ptr,beta_ptr,a_ptr,C,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
7	    pid=tl.program_id(0)
8	    offs_c=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C); offs_c2=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)
9	    mask=offs_c[:,None]>offs_c2[None,:]
10	    eye=tl.where(offs_c[:,None]==offs_c2[None,:],1.0,0.0)
11	    M=tl.load(m0_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:]).to(tl.float32)

+import torch
+import triton, triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def test_beta(b_ptr,o1_ptr,o2_ptr,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
+    beta=tl.load(b_ptr+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)).to(tl.float32)
+    o1=beta[:,None]
+    o2=beta[None,:]
+    tl.store(o1_ptr+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[:,None]*BLOCK_C+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[None,:],o1)
+    tl.store(o2_ptr+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[:,None]*BLOCK_C+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[None,:],o2)
+
+C=4
+device='cuda'
+beta=torch.tensor([1.0,2.0,3.0,4.0],device=device,dtype=torch.float32)
+o1=torch.empty(C,C,device=device,dtype=torch.float32)
+o2=torch.empty(C,C,device=device,dtype=torch.float32)
+test_beta[(1,)](beta,o1,o2,C)
+print("beta[:,None]\n",o1)
+print("beta[None,:]\n",o2)

+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260619_035957_kimi-claude_kimi-k2.7-code_02_kda_cutlass/repo/problems/02_kda_cutlass/scratch_beta_mul_test.py

+import torch
+import triton, triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def beta_mul_test(m0_ptr,b_ptr,o_ptr,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
+    pid=tl.program_id(0)
+    offs_c=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C); offs_c2=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)
+    M=tl.load(m0_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:]).to(tl.float32)
+    beta=tl.load(b_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C).to(tl.float32)
+    O=M*beta[:,None]
+    tl.store(o_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:],O.to(tl.bfloat16))
+

+import torch
+import triton, triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def beta_mul_const(b_ptr,o_ptr,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
+    beta=tl.load(b_ptr+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)).to(tl.float32)
+    M=tl.ones((BLOCK_C,BLOCK_C),dtype=tl.float32)
+    O=M*beta[:,None]
+    tl.store(o_ptr+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[:,None]*BLOCK_C+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[None,:],O.to(tl.bfloat16))
+
+if __name__=="__main__":

+    O=torch.empty(C,C,device=device,dtype=torch.bfloat16)

+    print(O.to(torch.float32))

5	def beta_mul_test(m0_ptr,b_ptr,o_ptr,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
6	    pid=tl.program_id(0)
7	    offs_c=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C); offs_c2=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)
8	    M=tl.load(m0_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:]).to(tl.float32)
9	    beta=tl.load(b_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C).to(tl.float32)
10	    O=M*beta[:,None]
11	    tl.store(o_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:],O.to(tl.bfloat16))
12

16	    tl.store(o_ptr+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[:,None]*BLOCK_C+tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)[None,:],beta[:,None])

1	"""Custom Triton + batched-GEMM Kimi Delta Attention forward (chunk form).
2	
3	The implementation is split into three phases:
4	1. Build the per-chunk lower-triangular A matrix via repeated squaring in a
5	   small Triton kernel (parallel over all chunks).
6	2. Compute w = A @ k_pos, u = A @ v, and Aqk = masked(qtilde @ k_neg^T) with
7	   torch.bmm (batched over all chunks/heads).
8	3. Run the inter-chunk recurrence in a Triton kernel that processes V-tiles in
9	   parallel and loops over chunks sequentially per (batch, head).
10	
11	This avoids calling any FLA KDA routine and is a real custom kernel.
12	"""
13	from __future__ import annotations
14	
15	import torch
16	import torch.nn as nn
17	import triton

A_loop entries can be up to ~9 under stress; bf16 precision okay. We could store fp32 for accuracy, but then bmm A@v uses fp32 A with bf16 v? torch.bmm supports fp32 A @ bf16 v? It may upcast. But A fp32 better. Let's store A_partial as fp32. The recurrence kernel uses A_bf; we can cast in Python. Store as fp32 avoids quantization. Then later cast to bf16 for bmm and recurrence. Actually we need A for w,u (bmm). bmm with A fp32 and k_pos bf16 will produce fp32 output. Good. For recurrence kernel, we can pass A_fp32 and cast to bf16 inside. But storing fp32 uses more memory. Fine. Let's store A_partial as fp32. Modify store to not cast. Then Python multiply by beta_col (fp32). Then A is fp32. Use for bmm. For recurrence kernel, we pass A_fp32; kernel casts to bf16. 209	
210	class Model(nn.Module):
211	    """KDA forward (chunk form) via custom Triton kernels + batched GEMMs."""
212	
213	    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
214	        super().__init__()
215	        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
216	        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
217	        self.scale = float(K) ** -0.5
218	        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1), persistent=False)
219	
220	    def forward(
221	        self,
222	        q: torch.Tensor,
223	        k: torch.Tensor,
224	        v: torch.Tensor,
225	        g: torch.Tensor,
226	        beta: torch.Tensor,
227	    ) -> torch.Tensor:
228	        B, T, H, K = q.shape
229	        V = v.shape[-1]
230	        C = self.chunk_size
231	        N = T // C
232	        scale = self.scale
233	
234	        # Chunk layout: (B, H, N, C, D) -- contiguous for batched GEMMs.
235	        q = rearrange(q, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=C).contiguous()
236	        k = rearrange(k, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=C).contiguous()
237	        v = rearrange(v, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=C).contiguous()
238	        g = rearrange(g, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=C).contiguous()

import torch
from einops import rearrange
import solution
B,T,H,K,V=2,1024,8,128,128
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42); torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(42)
q=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,T,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))

# run through solution forward up to A
import reference
reference.B,reference.T,reference.H,reference.K,reference.V,reference.CHUNK_SIZE=B,T,H,K,V,64
refm=reference.Model(B,T,H,K,V).to(device).eval()
solm=solution.Model(B,T,H,K,V).to(device).eval()
# monkey patch forward to expose A? easier replicate manually
C=64; N=T//C
scale=K**-0.5
q2=rearrange(q.to(torch.float32)*scale,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=C)
k2=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=C)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=C).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=C)
kpos=k2*G.exp(); kneg=k2*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
mask=torch.arange(C,device=device)[None,:,None]>=torch.arange(C,device=device)[None,None,:]
M0=M0*mask
# ref A
Aref=M0.clone()
Aref=Aref*betaR[...,None]
Aref=-Aref
for i in range(1,C):
    Aref[:,:,:,i,:i]=Aref[:,:,:,i,:i]+(Aref[:,:,:,i,:,None]*Aref[:,:,:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
Aref=(Aref+torch.eye(C,device=device))*betaR[...,None,:]
# solution A via closure kernel
flat=B*H*N
M=-M0.reshape(flat,C,C)*betaR.reshape(flat,C)[:,:,None]
Apartial=torch.empty(flat,C,C,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)
solution._closure_kernel[(flat,)](M,Apartial,flat,C,M.stride(0),M.stride(1),M.stride(2),Apartial.stride(0),Apartial.stride(1),Apartial.stride(2),BLOCK_C=C)
A2=(Apartial*betaR.reshape(flat,C)[:,None,:]).reshape(B,H,N,C,C)
print("A diff max",(Aref-A2).abs().max().item())
print("A ref max",Aref.abs().max().item(),"A2 max",A2.abs().max().item())

import torch
from einops import rearrange
BT=64
B,H,N,K,V=2,8,16,128,128
scale=K**-0.5
device='cuda'
torch.manual_seed(42)
q=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
k=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=device)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,N*BT,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=device))
q=rearrange(q.to(torch.float32)*scale,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
k=rearrange(k.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
G=rearrange(g,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
betaR=rearrange(beta.to(torch.float32),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
kpos=k*G.exp(); kneg=k*(-G).exp()
M0=torch.matmul(kpos,kneg.transpose(-1,-2))
mask=torch.arange(BT,device=device)[None,:,None]>=torch.arange(BT,device=device)[None,None,:]

# fp64 solve
flat=B*H*N
M0d=M0.reshape(flat,BT,BT).to(torch.float64)
bd=betaR.reshape(flat,BT).to(torch.float64)
I=torch.eye(BT,device=device,dtype=torch.float64).unsqueeze(0).expand(flat,-1,-1)
X=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I+M0d*bd[:,:,None],I,upper=False)
A2=(X*bd[:,None,:]).to(torch.float32).reshape(B,H,N,BT,BT)
print("fp64 diff",(A-A2).abs().max().item())
print("A max",A.abs().max().item(),"A2 max",A2.abs().max().item())

    A[:,:,:,i,:i]=A[:,:,:,i,:i]+(A[:,:,:,i,:,None]*A[:,:,:,:,:i]).sum(-2)
A=(A+torch.eye(BT,device=device))*betaR[...,None,:]
flat=B*H*N
M0f=M0.reshape(flat,BT,BT)
bf=betaR.reshape(flat,BT)
I=torch.eye(BT,device=device).unsqueeze(0).expand(flat,-1,-1)
X=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I+M0f*bf[:,:,None],I,upper=False)
A2=(X*bf[:,None,:]).reshape(B,H,N,BT,BT)
print("diff",(A-A2).abs().max().item())
print("A max",A.abs().max().item(),"A2 max",A2.abs().max().item())

reasoning (1785 chars)
Solve fails even for C=8. The issue is fundamental: solve_triangular does not compute the inverse of (I+M) for this lower triangular M because M has large entries and the matrix is not diagonally dominant; forward substitution in solve_triangular accumulates errors catastrophically? But manual forward substitution works. Maybe torch.linalg.solve_triangular uses a different algorithm (e.g., blocked) that is unstable for these matrices. We cannot rely on it. Thus we need a correct Triton forward substitution. The bug was likely `tl.where(row_mask, new_row[None,:], M)` orientation. We need ensure it updates row i. We can test by writing a closure kernel that uses `tl.store` to write row i explicitly into a flat M buffer, but M is in registers. Alternatively, use `M = M + tl.where(row_mask, new_row[None,:] - row_i_orig, 0.0)` but same orientation. Maybe the issue is `row_mask` shape (C,1) and `new_row[None,:]` shape (1,C). Triton broadcasting treats both as (C,C) but aligns singleton dims oppositely, resulting in a mask that is actually column i (because row_mask is treated as (1,C)). To force row mask, we can make row_mask shape (C,C) explicitly via `row_mask = (offs_c[:,None] == i) & (offs_c2[None,:] < BLOCK_C)`? But `offs_c2[None,:] < BLOCK_C` is all True, shape (1,C). Combined with (C,1) gives (C,C) with row i True. However Triton may still treat the combined mask orientation weirdly. We can test. Actually, if `tl.where(row_mask, X, M)` updates column i, we can use the same logic to update row i by using `tl.where(col_mask, ...)` where col_mask intended as row? Confusing. Let's test in a small Triton kernel: create a matrix M of 0..15, set row 2 to all 9s using `tl.where(row_mask, 9, M)` with row_mask = offs_c[:,None]==2. See if row or column changes.

+import torch
+import triton, triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def set_row(m_ptr,o_ptr,row_idx,BLOCK_C:tl.constexpr):
+    pid=tl.program_id(0)
+    offs_c=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C); offs_c2=tl.arange(0,BLOCK_C)
+    M=tl.load(m_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:]).to(tl.float32)
+    mask=offs_c[:,None]==row_idx
+    O=tl.where(mask,tl.full((BLOCK_C,BLOCK_C),9.0,dtype=tl.float32),M)
+    tl.store(o_ptr+pid*BLOCK_C*BLOCK_C+offs_c[:,None]*BLOCK_C+offs_c2[None,:],O.to(tl.bfloat16))
+
+C=4; device='cuda'
+M=torch.arange(C*C,device=device,dtype=torch.float32).reshape(1,C,C)
+O=torch.empty(1,C,C,device=device,dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+set_row[(1,)](M,O,2,C)
+print(O.to(torch.float32)[0])
